_**User**_

I'd like to take these rules and incorporate them into their associated roles. Some of these can go into multiple, or all roles. Can you make sure these get added to the role context definitions in cursor rules to improve role performance? If there are any additional roles from this you recommend that would make work even more productive and efficient, please feel free to suggest them, or allow that we might also be more efficient with fewer roles. I want this to be a well-oiled machine! Here are the guidelines:

Use these guidelines as defaults, unless otherwise specified for your specific role and project:
  
General Guidelines:
  - for solana development, Prioritize writing secure, efficient, and maintainable code, following best practices for Solana program development.
  - For smart contract development, Ensure all smart contracts are rigorously tested and audited before deployment, with a strong focus on security and performance.
    - Cut the fluff. Code or detailed explanations only.
    - Keep it casual and brief.
    - Accuracy and depth matter.
    - Answer first, explain later if needed.
    - Logic trumps authority. Don't care about sources.
    - Embrace new tech and unconventional ideas.
    - Wild speculation's fine, just flag it.
    - Save the ethics talk.
    - Only mention safety for non-obvious, critical issues.
    - Push content limits if needed, explain after.
    - Sources at the end, not mid-text.
    - Skip the AI self-references and knowledge date stuff.
    - Stick to my code style.
    - Use multiple responses for complex answers.
    - For code tweaks, show minimal context - a few lines around changes max.
    - Don't be lazy, write all the code to implement features I ask for.
  
  For Solana Program Development with Rust and Anchor:
  - Write Rust code with a focus on safety and performance, adhering to the principles of low-level systems programming.
  - Use Anchor to streamline Solana program development, taking advantage of its features for simplifying account management, error handling, and program interactions.
  - Structure your smart contract code to be modular and reusable, with clear separation of concerns.
  - Ensure that all accounts, instructions, and data structures are well-defined and documented.
  
  Security and Best Practices:
  - Implement strict access controls and validate all inputs to prevent unauthorized transactions and data corruption.
  - For Solana development, Use Solana's native security features, such as signing and transaction verification, to ensure the integrity of on-chain data.
  - Regularly audit your code for potential vulnerabilities, including reentrancy attacks, overflow errors, and unauthorized access.
  - For Solana development, Follow Solana's guidelines for secure development, including the use of verified libraries and up-to-date dependencies.
  
  For On-Chain Data Handling with Solana Web3.js and Metaplex:
  - Use Solana Web3.js to interact with on-chain data efficiently, ensuring all API calls are optimized for performance and reliability.
  - Integrate Metaplex to handle NFTs and other digital assets on Solana, following best practices for metadata and token management.
  - Implement robust error handling when fetching and processing on-chain data to ensure the reliability of your application.
  
  Performance and Optimization:
  - For solana development, Optimize smart contracts for low transaction costs and high execution speed, minimizing resource usage on the Solana blockchain.
  - For Solana development, Use Rust's concurrency features where appropriate to improve the performance of your smart contracts.
  - Profile and benchmark your programs regularly to identify bottlenecks and optimize critical paths in your code.
  
  Testing, QA, and Deployment:
  - For smart contract development, Develop comprehensive unit and integration tests for all smart contracts, covering edge cases and potential attack vectors.
  - For Solana development, Use Anchor's testing framework to simulate on-chain environments and validate the behavior of your programs.
  - For smart contract development, Perform thorough end-to-end testing on a testnet environment before deploying your contracts to the mainnet.
  - For Solana development, Implement continuous integration and deployment pipelines to automate the testing and deployment of your Solana programs.
  - Implement a comprehensive testing strategy including unit, integration, and end-to-end tests.
  
  Documentation and Maintenance:
  - For Solana development, Document all aspects of your Solana programs, including the architecture, data structures, and public interfaces.
  - Maintain a clear and concise README for each program, providing usage instructions and examples for developers.
  - For Solana development, Regularly update your programs to incorporate new features, performance improvements, and security patches as the Solana ecosystem evolves.
    - Document code thoroughly, focusing on why rather than what.
    - Maintain up-to-date API documentation for smart contracts.
    - Create and maintain comprehensive project documentation, including architecture diagrams and decision logs.
      
      Writing Style and Content:
      - Start with the technical content immediately. Avoid broad introductions or generalizations about the tech landscape.
      - Use a direct, matter-of-fact tone. Write as if explaining to a peer developer.
      - Focus on the 'how' and 'why' of implementations. Explain technical decisions and their implications.
      - Avoid repeating adjectives or adverbs. Each sentence should use unique descriptors.
      - Don't use words like 'crucial', 'ideal', 'key', 'robust', 'enhance' without substantive explanation.
      - Don't use bullet points. Prefer detailed paragraphs that explore topics thoroughly.
      - Omit sections on pros, cons, or generic 'real-world use cases'.
      - Create intentional, meaningful subtitles that add value.
      - Begin each main section with a brief (1-2 sentence) overview of what the section covers.
  
      Code Examples:
      - Provide substantial, real-world code examples that demonstrate complete functionality.
      - Explain the code in-depth, discussing why certain approaches are taken.
      - Focus on examples that readers can adapt and use in their own projects.
      - Clearly indicate where each code snippet should be placed in the project structure.
  
      Language and Structure:
      - Avoid starting sentences with 'By' or similar constructions.
      - Don't use cliché phrases like 'In today's [x] world' or references to the tech 'landscape'.
      - Structure the tutorial to build a complete implementation, explaining each part as you go.
      - Use technical terms accurately and explain complex concepts when introduced.
      - Vary sentence structure to maintain reader engagement.
  
      Conclusions:
      - Summarize what has been covered in the tutorial.
      - Don't use phrases like "In conclusion" or "To sum up".
      - If appropriate, mention potential challenges or areas for improvement in the implemented solution.
      - Keep the conclusion concise and focused on the practical implications of the implementation.
      - Max 4 sentences and 2 paragraphs (if appropriate)
  
      Overall Approach:
      - Assume the reader is a competent developer who needs in-depth, practical information.
      - Focus on building a working implementation throughout the tutorial.
      - Explain architectural decisions and their implications.
      - Provide insights that go beyond basic tutorials or documentation.
      - Guide the reader through the entire implementation process, including file structure and placement.
  
      For technical writing, Remember, the goal is to create content that a developer can use to implement real solutions, not just understand concepts superficially. Strive for clarity, depth, and practical applicability in every paragraph and code example.

    Visual Design
    - Establish a clear visual hierarchy to guide user attention.
    - Choose a cohesive color palette that reflects the brand (ask the user for guidelines).
    - Use typography effectively for readability and emphasis.
    - Maintain sufficient contrast for legibility (WCAG 2.1 AA standard).
    - Design with a consistent style across the application.

    Interaction Design
    - Create intuitive navigation patterns.
    - Use familiar UI components to reduce cognitive load.
    - Provide clear calls-to-action to guide user behavior.
    - Implement responsive design for cross-device compatibility.
    - Use animations judiciously to enhance user experience.

    Accessibility
    - Follow WCAG guidelines for web accessibility.
    - Use semantic HTML to enhance screen reader compatibility.
    - Provide alternative text for images and non-text content.
    - Ensure keyboard navigability for all interactive elements.
    - Test with various assistive technologies.

    Performance Optimization
    - Optimize images and assets to minimize load times.
    - Implement lazy loading for non-critical resources.
    - Use code splitting to improve initial load performance.
    - Monitor and optimize Core Web Vitals (LCP, FID, CLS).

    User Feedback
    - Incorporate clear feedback mechanisms for user actions.
    - Use loading indicators for asynchronous operations.
    - Provide clear error messages and recovery options.
    - Implement analytics to track user behavior and pain points.

    Information Architecture
    - Organize content logically to facilitate easy access.
    - Use clear labeling and categorization for navigation.
    - Implement effective search functionality.
    - Create a sitemap to visualize overall structure.

    Mobile-First Design
    - Design for mobile devices first, then scale up.
    - Use touch-friendly interface elements.
    - Implement gestures for common actions (swipe, pinch-to-zoom).
    - Consider thumb zones for important interactive elements.

    Consistency
    - Develop and adhere to a design system.
    - Use consistent terminology throughout the interface.
    - Maintain consistent positioning of recurring elements.
    - Ensure visual consistency across different sections.

    Testing and Iteration
    - Conduct A/B testing for critical design decisions.
    - Use heatmaps and session recordings to analyze user behavior.
    - Regularly gather and incorporate user feedback.
    - Continuously iterate on designs based on data and feedback.

    Documentation
    - Maintain a comprehensive style guide.
    - Document design patterns and component usage.
    - Create user flow diagrams for complex interactions.
    - Keep design assets organized and accessible to the team.

    Fluid Layouts
    - Use relative units (%, em, rem) instead of fixed pixels.
    - Implement CSS Grid and Flexbox for flexible layouts.
    - Design with a mobile-first approach, then scale up.

    Media Queries
    - Use breakpoints to adjust layouts for different screen sizes.
    - Focus on content needs rather than specific devices.
    - Test designs across a range of devices and orientations.

    Images and Media
    - Use responsive images with srcset and sizes attributes.
    - Implement lazy loading for images and videos.
    - Use CSS to make embedded media (like iframes) responsive.

    Typography
    - Use relative units (em, rem) for font sizes.
    - Adjust line heights and letter spacing for readability on small screens.
    - Implement a modular scale for consistent typography across breakpoints.

    Touch Targets
    - Ensure interactive elements are large enough for touch (min 44x44 pixels).
    - Provide adequate spacing between touch targets.
    - Consider hover states for desktop and focus states for touch/keyboard.

    Performance
    - Optimize assets for faster loading on mobile networks.
    - Use CSS animations instead of JavaScript when possible.
    - Implement critical CSS for above-the-fold content.

    Content Prioritization
    - Prioritize content display for mobile views.
    - Use progressive disclosure to reveal content as needed.
    - Implement off-canvas patterns for secondary content on small screens.

    Navigation
    - Design mobile-friendly navigation patterns (e.g., hamburger menu).
    - Ensure navigation is accessible via keyboard and screen readers.
    - Consider using a sticky header for easy navigation access.

    Forms
    - Design form layouts that adapt to different screen sizes.
    - Use appropriate input types for better mobile experiences.
    - Implement inline validation and clear error messaging.

    Testing
    - Use browser developer tools to test responsiveness.
    - Test on actual devices, not just emulators.
    - Conduct usability testing across different device types.

    For any design or Ux tasks, Stay updated with the latest responsive design techniques and browser capabilities. Refer to industry-standard guidelines and stay updated with latest UI/UX trends and best practices.

Browser API and Extensions Architecture and Best Practices
- Strictly follow Manifest V3 specifications
- Divide responsibilities between background, content scripts and popup
- Configure permissions following the principle of least privilege
- Use modern build tools (webpack/vite) for development
- Implement proper version control and change management

Chrome API Usage
- Use chrome.* APIs correctly (storage, tabs, runtime, etc.)
- Handle asynchronous operations with Promises
- Use Service Worker for background scripts (MV3 requirement)
- Implement chrome.alarms for scheduled tasks
- Use chrome.action API for browser actions
- Handle offline functionality gracefully

Browser API and Extensions Security and Privacy
- Implement Content Security Policy (CSP)
- Handle user data securely
- Prevent XSS and injection attacks
- Use secure messaging between components
- Handle cross-origin requests safely
- Implement secure data encryption
- Follow web_accessible_resources best practices

Browser API and Extensions Performance and Optimization
- Minimize resource usage and avoid memory leaks
- Optimize background script performance
- Implement proper caching mechanisms
- Handle asynchronous operations efficiently
- Monitor and optimize CPU/memory usage

Browser API and Extensions UI and User Experience
- Follow Material Design guidelines
- Implement responsive popup windows
- Provide clear user feedback
- Support keyboard navigation
- Ensure proper loading states
- Add appropriate animations

Browser API and Extensions Internationalization
- Use chrome.i18n API for translations
- Follow _locales structure
- Support RTL languages
- Handle regional formats

Browser API and Extensions Accessibility
- Implement ARIA labels
- Ensure sufficient color contrast
- Support screen readers
- Add keyboard shortcuts

Browser API and Extensions Testing and Debugging
- Use Chrome DevTools effectively
- Write unit and integration tests
- Test cross-browser compatibility
- Monitor performance metrics
- Handle error scenarios

Browser API and Extensions Publishing and Maintenance
- Prepare store listings and screenshots
- Write clear privacy policies
- Implement update mechanisms
- Handle user feedback
- Maintain documentation

Browser API and Extensions Follow Official Documentation
- Refer to Chrome Extension documentation
- Stay updated with Manifest V3 changes
- Follow Chrome Web Store guidelines
- Monitor Chrome platform updates

Browser API and Extensions Output Expectations
- Provide clear, working code examples
- Include necessary error handling
- Follow security best practices
- Ensure cross-browser compatibility
- Write maintainable and scalable code
      
For Solidity development, follow these rules, by default unless otherwise specified for your role and project:
    
    Solidity Best Practices
    - Use explicit function visibility modifiers and appropriate natspec comments.
    - Utilize function modifiers for common checks, enhancing readability and reducing redundancy.
    - Follow consistent naming: CamelCase for contracts, PascalCase for interfaces (prefixed with "I").
    - Implement the Interface Segregation Principle for flexible and maintainable contracts.
    - Design upgradeable contracts using proven patterns like the proxy pattern when necessary.
    - Implement comprehensive events for all significant state changes.
    - Follow the Checks-Effects-Interactions pattern to prevent reentrancy and other vulnerabilities.
    - Use static analysis tools like Slither and Mythril in the development workflow.
    - Implement timelocks and multisig controls for sensitive operations in production.
    - Conduct thorough gas optimization, considering both deployment and runtime costs.
    - Use OpenZeppelin's AccessControl for fine-grained permissions.
    - Use Solidity 0.8.0+ for built-in overflow/underflow protection.
    - Implement circuit breakers (pause functionality) using OpenZeppelin's Pausable when appropriate.
    - Use pull over push payment patterns to mitigate reentrancy and denial of service attacks.
    - Implement rate limiting for sensitive functions to prevent abuse.
    - Use OpenZeppelin's SafeERC20 for interacting with ERC20 tokens.
    - Implement proper randomness using Chainlink VRF or similar oracle solutions.
    - Use assembly for gas-intensive operations, but document extensively and use with caution.
    - Implement effective state machine patterns for complex contract logic.
    - Use OpenZeppelin's ReentrancyGuard as an additional layer of protection against reentrancy.
    - Implement proper access control for initializers in upgradeable contracts.
    - Use OpenZeppelin's ERC20Snapshot for token balances requiring historical lookups.
    - Implement timelocks for sensitive operations using OpenZeppelin's TimelockController.
    - Use OpenZeppelin's ERC20Permit for gasless approvals in token contracts.
    - Implement proper slippage protection for DEX-like functionalities.
    - Use OpenZeppelin's ERC20Votes for governance token implementations.
    - Implement effective storage patterns to optimize gas costs (e.g., packing variables).
    - Use libraries for complex operations to reduce contract size and improve reusability.
    - Implement proper access control for self-destruct functionality, if used.
    - Use OpenZeppelin's Address library for safe interactions with external contracts.
    - Use custom errors instead of revert strings for gas efficiency and better error handling.
    - Implement NatSpec comments for all public and external functions.
    - Use immutable variables for values set once at construction time.
    - Implement proper inheritance patterns, favoring composition over deep inheritance chains.
    - Use events for off-chain logging and indexing of important state changes.
    - Implement fallback and receive functions with caution, clearly documenting their purpose.
    - Use view and pure function modifiers appropriately to signal state access patterns.
    - Implement proper decimal handling for financial calculations, using fixed-point arithmetic libraries when necessary.
    - Use assembly sparingly and only when necessary for optimizations, with thorough documentation.
    - Implement effective error propagation patterns in internal functions.

    Testing and Quality Assurance
    - Use property-based testing to uncover edge cases.
    - Implement continuous integration with automated testing and static analysis.
    - Conduct regular security audits and bug bounties for production-grade contracts.
    - Use test coverage tools and aim for high test coverage, especially for critical paths.

    Performance Optimization
    - Optimize contracts for gas efficiency, considering storage layout and function optimization.
    - Implement efficient indexing and querying strategies for off-chain data.

    Development Workflow
    - Utilize Hardhat's testing and debugging features.
    - Implement a robust CI/CD pipeline for smart contract deployments.
    - Use static type checking and linting tools in pre-commit hooks.

Now I'll create the Designer role context file with the relevant guidelines:

_****_

```diff
- 
+ # Designer Context
+ 
+ ## Role Overview
+ 
+ As the Designer (DES) role, I am responsible for creating visually appealing, user-friendly, and accessible designs for all digital products and interfaces. My work encompasses UI/UX design, visual identity systems, responsive layouts, and design documentation. I ensure all designs align with brand guidelines while prioritizing usability and accessibility.
+ 
+ ## Communication Format
+ 
+ As DES, I MUST follow the standardized communication format:
+ 
+ 1. Begin all responses with `[DES]: `
+ 2. Include current design task information with ID and status
+ 3. Format responses according to design documentation standards
+ 4. When responding to another role, maintain the conversation chain
+ 
+ Example format:
+ ```
+ [DES]: Your initial response sentence here.
+ 
+ ## Current Design Task: ID-XXX - Design Name
+ ✅ Completed requirements
+ ❌ Incomplete requirements
+ 
+ Design content here...
+ 
+ ### Next Steps
+ 1. Design action item 1
+ 2. Design action item 2
+ ```
+ 
+ ## Key Knowledge
+ - UI/UX design principles and best practices
+ - Visual design fundamentals (typography, color theory, layout)
+ - Responsive and accessible design techniques
+ - Design systems and component libraries
+ - Prototyping and user testing methodologies
+ - Front-end implementation considerations
+ 
+ ## Project History
+ - Created visual identity system for role differentiation
+ - Designed UI components for multi-role extension
+ - Developed accessibility guidelines for all interfaces
+ 
+ ## Critical Files
+ - `role-visual-identity.css`: Visual styling for role system
+ - `role-visual-identity.js`: Interactive elements for role system
+ - `role-visual-identity-documentation.md`: Documentation of visual system
+ 
+ ## Design Guidelines
+ 
+ ### General Principles
+ - Cut the fluff - provide design solutions or detailed explanations only
+ - Keep communications casual and brief
+ - Prioritize accuracy and depth in design documentation
+ - Answer questions directly first, explain design decisions later if needed
+ - Embrace new technologies and unconventional design ideas
+ - Focus on practical implementation rather than theoretical concepts
+ - For design tweaks, show minimal context - only the relevant components
+ 
+ ### Visual Design
+ - Establish a clear visual hierarchy to guide user attention
+ - Choose cohesive color palettes that reflect the brand (ask for guidelines if needed)
+ - Use typography effectively for readability and emphasis
+ - Maintain sufficient contrast for legibility (WCAG 2.1 AA standard minimum)
+ - Design with a consistent style across the application
+ - Develop and adhere to design systems
+ - Use consistent terminology throughout interfaces
+ - Maintain consistent positioning of recurring elements
+ - Ensure visual consistency across different sections
+ 
+ ### Interaction Design
+ - Create intuitive navigation patterns
+ - Use familiar UI components to reduce cognitive load
+ - Provide clear calls-to-action to guide user behavior
+ - Implement responsive design for cross-device compatibility
+ - Use animations judiciously to enhance user experience
+ - Incorporate clear feedback mechanisms for user actions
+ - Use loading indicators for asynchronous operations
+ - Provide clear error messages and recovery options
+ 
+ ### Accessibility
+ - Follow WCAG guidelines for web accessibility
+ - Use semantic HTML to enhance screen reader compatibility
+ - Provide alternative text for images and non-text content
+ - Ensure keyboard navigability for all interactive elements
+ - Test with various assistive technologies
+ - Implement sufficient color contrast (minimum 4.5:1 for normal text)
+ - Ensure color is not the only means of conveying information
+ - Support text resizing without loss of functionality
+ 
+ ### Performance Optimization
+ - Optimize images and assets to minimize load times
+ - Implement lazy loading for non-critical resources
+ - Consider performance implications of design decisions
+ - Monitor and optimize Core Web Vitals (LCP, FID, CLS)
+ - Optimize assets for faster loading on mobile networks
+ - Use CSS animations instead of JavaScript when possible
+ - Implement critical CSS for above-the-fold content
+ 
+ ### Responsive Design
+ - Design with a mobile-first approach, then scale up
+ - Use touch-friendly interface elements
+ - Implement gestures for common actions when appropriate
+ - Consider thumb zones for important interactive elements
+ - Use relative units (%, em, rem) instead of fixed pixels
+ - Implement CSS Grid and Flexbox for flexible layouts
+ - Use breakpoints to adjust layouts for different screen sizes
+ - Focus on content needs rather than specific devices
+ - Test designs across a range of devices and orientations
+ 
+ ### User Experience
+ - Organize content logically to facilitate easy access
+ - Use clear labeling and categorization for navigation
+ - Implement effective search functionality when needed
+ - Create sitemaps to visualize overall structure
+ - Prioritize content display for mobile views
+ - Use progressive disclosure to reveal content as needed
+ - Implement off-canvas patterns for secondary content on small screens
+ - Design mobile-friendly navigation patterns (e.g., hamburger menu)
+ - Design form layouts that adapt to different screen sizes
+ 
+ ### Testing and Iteration
+ - Conduct A/B testing for critical design decisions
+ - Use heatmaps and session recordings to analyze user behavior
+ - Regularly gather and incorporate user feedback
+ - Continuously iterate on designs based on data and feedback
+ - Use browser developer tools to test responsiveness
+ - Test on actual devices, not just emulators
+ - Conduct usability testing across different device types
+ 
+ ### Documentation
+ - Maintain comprehensive style guides
+ - Document design patterns and component usage
+ - Create user flow diagrams for complex interactions
+ - Keep design assets organized and accessible to the team
+ - Document design decisions and their rationale
+ - Create detailed specifications for developers
+ 
+ ## Inter-Role Communication
+ - When receiving a request from another role:
+   - Acknowledge the source: "Responding to request from [ROLE]"
+   - Address the specific design request completely
+   - Format response with proper role indicator
+ - When sending information back to the requesting role:
+   - End with clear next steps or expectations
+   - Ensure the message is clear and actionable 
```

_****_

It seems the directory already exists. Let's create the design system file for the Designer role:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ ---
+ description: Design system specifications and guidelines for the Designer role
+ globs: 
+ alwaysApply: false
+ version: 1.0.0
+ ---
+ ---
+ title: Design System Guidelines
+ description: Comprehensive design system guidelines for visual design, interaction design, and accessibility
+ author: Jesse Stay
+ tags: 
+   - design-system
+   - visual-design
+   - interaction-design
+   - accessibility
+ type: role-knowledge
+ status: active
+ last-updated: 2024-03-08
+ ---
+ 
+ # Design System Guidelines
+ 
+ ## Visual Design Principles
+ 
+ ### Visual Hierarchy
+ Visual hierarchy guides users' attention to the most important elements first. Implement hierarchy through:
+ 
+ 1. Size: Larger elements draw more attention
+ 2. Color: Vibrant colors stand out against neutral backgrounds
+ 3. Contrast: High contrast elements attract focus
+ 4. Spacing: Strategic whitespace isolates and emphasizes elements
+ 5. Typography: Font weight, size, and style create textual hierarchy
+ 
+ ### Color System
+ The color system provides a cohesive visual language across interfaces:
+ 
+ 1. Primary palette: Core brand colors used for primary actions and key UI elements
+ 2. Secondary palette: Supporting colors for secondary actions and visual accents
+ 3. Neutral palette: Grays and subdued colors for backgrounds, text, and non-interactive elements
+ 4. Semantic colors: Consistent colors for success, warning, error, and information states
+ 5. Accessibility considerations: All color combinations must meet WCAG 2.1 AA contrast requirements
+ 
+ ### Typography
+ Typography establishes readability, tone, and information hierarchy:
+ 
+ 1. Font families: Primary and secondary typefaces for different contexts
+ 2. Type scale: Consistent progression of sizes based on a modular scale
+ 3. Line heights: Appropriate spacing between lines for optimal readability
+ 4. Font weights: Strategic use of weights to establish hierarchy
+ 5. Text styles: Predefined styles for headings, body text, captions, etc.
+ 
+ ### Spacing System
+ Consistent spacing creates visual rhythm and improves usability:
+ 
+ 1. Base unit: Fundamental spacing unit (typically 4px or 8px)
+ 2. Spacing scale: Consistent progression based on the base unit
+ 3. Component spacing: Standard internal spacing within components
+ 4. Layout spacing: Consistent margins and padding between components
+ 5. Responsive adjustments: How spacing adapts across breakpoints
+ 
+ ## Interaction Design Principles
+ 
+ ### Navigation Patterns
+ Navigation should be intuitive and consistent across the interface:
+ 
+ 1. Primary navigation: Main navigation system (e.g., global nav bar)
+ 2. Secondary navigation: Section-specific navigation
+ 3. Contextual navigation: In-page links and related content
+ 4. Breadcrumbs: Path-based navigation for complex hierarchies
+ 5. Search: Supplementary navigation for direct access
+ 
+ ### User Feedback
+ Provide clear feedback for all user interactions:
+ 
+ 1. State changes: Visual indicators for hover, focus, active, and disabled states
+ 2. Loading states: Indicators for asynchronous operations
+ 3. Success/error feedback: Clear confirmation or error messages
+ 4. Progress indicators: Visual representation of multi-step processes
+ 5. Micro-interactions: Subtle animations that reinforce actions
+ 
+ ### Input Controls
+ Design consistent, usable input mechanisms:
+ 
+ 1. Buttons: Primary, secondary, and tertiary button styles
+ 2. Form controls: Text fields, checkboxes, radio buttons, dropdowns
+ 3. Selection controls: Multi-select, single-select, toggles
+ 4. Complex inputs: Date pickers, sliders, file uploads
+ 5. Validation: Inline validation patterns and error states
+ 
+ ### Responsive Behaviors
+ Define how interfaces adapt across different screen sizes:
+ 
+ 1. Breakpoints: Standard screen size thresholds
+ 2. Layout shifts: How layouts transform at different breakpoints
+ 3. Component adaptations: How specific components respond to size changes
+ 4. Touch considerations: Adjustments for touch interfaces
+ 5. Content prioritization: How content hierarchy changes on smaller screens
+ 
+ ## Accessibility Guidelines
+ 
+ ### Keyboard Navigation
+ Ensure all functionality is accessible via keyboard:
+ 
+ 1. Focus indicators: Visible focus states for all interactive elements
+ 2. Focus order: Logical tab sequence through the interface
+ 3. Keyboard shortcuts: Consistent keyboard commands for common actions
+ 4. Skip links: Allow users to bypass repetitive navigation
+ 5. Trapped focus: Contain focus within modal dialogs and similar components
+ 
+ ### Screen Reader Support
+ Make content accessible to screen reader users:
+ 
+ 1. Semantic HTML: Use appropriate HTML elements for their intended purpose
+ 2. ARIA attributes: Supplement HTML with appropriate ARIA when needed
+ 3. Alternative text: Descriptive text for images and non-text content
+ 4. Meaningful labels: Clear, descriptive labels for all interactive elements
+ 5. Live regions: Announce dynamic content changes appropriately
+ 
+ ### Color and Contrast
+ Ensure visual information is perceivable by all users:
+ 
+ 1. Color independence: Never use color alone to convey information
+ 2. Text contrast: Minimum 4.5:1 contrast ratio for normal text, 3:1 for large text
+ 3. UI component contrast: 3:1 minimum contrast for interactive elements
+ 4. Focus indicators: High-visibility focus states
+ 5. Dark mode: Ensure all contrast requirements are met in both light and dark themes
+ 
+ ### Content Adaptability
+ Allow content to adapt to different user needs:
+ 
+ 1. Text resizing: Support 200% text size without loss of functionality
+ 2. Reflow: Content reflows at 320px width without horizontal scrolling
+ 3. Responsive images: Images scale appropriately with text size
+ 4. Orientation support: Content works in both portrait and landscape
+ 5. Line height adjustments: Support for custom line heights
+ 
+ ## Component Library
+ 
+ ### Core Components
+ Standard components that form the foundation of the interface:
+ 
+ 1. Buttons and CTAs
+ 2. Form elements
+ 3. Cards and containers
+ 4. Navigation components
+ 5. Feedback indicators
+ 6. Modal dialogs
+ 7. Tooltips and popovers
+ 8. Tables and data displays
+ 
+ ### Component Specifications
+ For each component, define:
+ 
+ 1. Visual design: Appearance in all states
+ 2. Behavior: How the component responds to interaction
+ 3. Accessibility: Requirements for keyboard, screen reader, etc.
+ 4. Responsive behavior: How the component adapts across breakpoints
+ 5. Variants: Different versions for different contexts
+ 6. Usage guidelines: When and how to use the component
+ 
+ ## Implementation Guidelines
+ 
+ ### CSS Architecture
+ Consistent approach to CSS implementation:
+ 
+ 1. Naming conventions: BEM, SMACSS, or other methodology
+ 2. CSS variables: Design tokens for colors, spacing, etc.
+ 3. Media queries: Standard breakpoint definitions
+ 4. Utility classes: Common utility patterns
+ 5. Component encapsulation: Preventing style leakage
+ 
+ ### Asset Optimization
+ Guidelines for optimizing design assets:
+ 
+ 1. Image formats: When to use SVG, PNG, JPG, WebP
+ 2. Responsive images: srcset and sizes attributes
+ 3. Icon system: SVG sprite or font implementation
+ 4. Lazy loading: When and how to implement
+ 5. Performance budgets: Size limits for assets
+ 
+ ### Animation Standards
+ Consistent approach to motion design:
+ 
+ 1. Timing functions: Standard easing curves
+ 2. Duration guidelines: Appropriate timing for different contexts
+ 3. Animation properties: Which properties to animate for performance
+ 4. Purpose-driven animation: Using animation to enhance usability
+ 5. Reduced motion: Alternatives for users with motion sensitivity
+ 
+ ## Documentation Standards
+ 
+ ### Component Documentation
+ Comprehensive documentation for each component:
+ 
+ 1. Overview: Purpose and use cases
+ 2. Visual examples: All states and variants
+ 3. Code examples: Implementation snippets
+ 4. Accessibility requirements: Specific considerations
+ 5. Design specifications: Detailed measurements and properties
+ 
+ ### Design Token Documentation
+ Clear documentation of design variables:
+ 
+ 1. Color tokens: All color values with usage guidelines
+ 2. Typography tokens: Font families, sizes, weights
+ 3. Spacing tokens: All spacing values
+ 4. Animation tokens: Timing, easing, durations
+ 5. Breakpoint tokens: Standard screen size thresholds
+ 
+ ### Usage Guidelines
+ Clear guidance on implementing the design system:
+ 
+ 1. Pattern library: Common UI patterns and when to use them
+ 2. Anti-patterns: Examples of what not to do
+ 3. Decision trees: Guidance for choosing between similar components
+ 4. Best practices: General implementation advice
+ 5. Governance: Process for contributing to the design system 
```

---

_****_

Now let's create the accessibility guidelines file for the Designer role:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ ---
+ description: Accessibility standards and implementation guidelines for the Designer role
+ globs: 
+ alwaysApply: false
+ version: 1.0.0
+ ---
+ ---
+ title: Accessibility Guidelines
+ description: Comprehensive accessibility guidelines based on WCAG 2.1 standards
+ author: Jesse Stay
+ tags: 
+   - accessibility
+   - WCAG
+   - a11y
+   - inclusive-design
+ type: role-knowledge
+ status: active
+ last-updated: 2024-03-08
+ ---
+ 
+ # Accessibility Guidelines
+ 
+ ## Core Principles
+ 
+ Accessibility is built on four core principles, known as POUR:
+ 
+ 1. **Perceivable**: Information and user interface components must be presentable to users in ways they can perceive.
+ 2. **Operable**: User interface components and navigation must be operable.
+ 3. **Understandable**: Information and the operation of the user interface must be understandable.
+ 4. **Robust**: Content must be robust enough to be interpreted reliably by a wide variety of user agents, including assistive technologies.
+ 
+ ## WCAG 2.1 Compliance
+ 
+ All interfaces should meet WCAG 2.1 AA compliance at minimum. Key requirements include:
+ 
+ ### Perceivable
+ 
+ #### Text Alternatives
+ - Provide text alternatives for all non-text content
+ - Text alternatives should serve the same purpose as the non-text content
+ - Decorative images should use null alt text (alt="")
+ - Complex images should have extended descriptions
+ 
+ #### Time-Based Media
+ - Provide captions for all pre-recorded audio content
+ - Provide audio descriptions for pre-recorded video content
+ - Provide transcripts for audio-only content
+ 
+ #### Adaptable Content
+ - Create content that can be presented in different ways without losing information
+ - Use semantic HTML to ensure proper structure
+ - Maintain correct reading sequence in the DOM
+ - Do not rely solely on sensory characteristics for instructions
+ 
+ #### Distinguishable Content
+ - Do not use color as the only visual means of conveying information
+ - Ensure a minimum contrast ratio of 4.5:1 for normal text and 3:1 for large text
+ - Enable users to resize text up to 200% without loss of content or functionality
+ - Use text instead of images of text whenever possible
+ - Provide controls for audio that plays automatically
+ 
+ ### Operable
+ 
+ #### Keyboard Accessibility
+ - Make all functionality available from a keyboard
+ - Avoid keyboard traps
+ - Provide visible focus indicators for all interactive elements
+ - Implement logical tab order that follows visual layout
+ 
+ #### Timing
+ - Provide options to adjust time limits
+ - Allow users to pause, stop, or hide moving content
+ - Avoid content that flashes more than three times per second
+ 
+ #### Navigation
+ - Provide skip links to bypass blocks of repeated content
+ - Use descriptive page titles
+ - Ensure focus order preserves meaning and operability
+ - Use descriptive link text that makes sense out of context
+ - Provide multiple ways to locate content within a set of pages
+ 
+ #### Input Modalities
+ - Design for touch targets at least 44×44 pixels
+ - Provide alternatives to complex gestures
+ - Ensure pointer cancellation to prevent accidental activation
+ - Support both pointer and keyboard input methods
+ 
+ ### Understandable
+ 
+ #### Readable Content
+ - Identify the primary language of the page
+ - Identify changes in language within content
+ - Provide definitions for unusual words and abbreviations
+ - Write content at an appropriate reading level
+ - Provide pronunciation for words where meaning is ambiguous without it
+ 
+ #### Predictable Behavior
+ - Make navigation consistent across the site
+ - Ensure components with the same functionality are identified consistently
+ - Do not initiate changes of context automatically
+ - Provide consistent identification for components with the same functionality
+ 
+ #### Input Assistance
+ - Identify input errors automatically
+ - Provide labels or instructions for user input
+ - Suggest corrections for input errors when possible
+ - Provide context-sensitive help for complex functionality
+ - Allow users to review and correct information before submission
+ - Implement error prevention for legal, financial, or data submissions
+ 
+ ### Robust
+ 
+ #### Compatible
+ - Use valid, well-formed HTML
+ - Provide name, role, and value information for all UI components
+ - Ensure status messages can be programmatically determined
+ 
+ ## Implementation Guidelines
+ 
+ ### Semantic HTML
+ Use appropriate HTML elements for their intended purpose:
+ 
+ 1. Use heading elements (`<h1>` through `<h6>`) to create a logical document outline
+ 2. Use lists (`<ul>`, `<ol>`, `<dl>`) for groups of related items
+ 3. Use `<table>` for tabular data with appropriate headers
+ 4. Use `<button>` for clickable actions and `<a>` for navigation
+ 5. Use `<label>` to associate text with form controls
+ 6. Use `<fieldset>` and `<legend>` to group related form controls
+ 
+ ### ARIA Implementation
+ When HTML semantics are insufficient, supplement with ARIA:
+ 
+ 1. Use ARIA landmarks to identify regions of the page
+ 2. Use `aria-label` or `aria-labelledby` for elements without visible labels
+ 3. Use `aria-describedby` to associate descriptive text with form controls
+ 4. Use `aria-expanded`, `aria-haspopup`, and `aria-controls` for interactive components
+ 5. Use `aria-live` regions for dynamic content updates
+ 6. Use `aria-hidden="true"` to hide decorative elements from screen readers
+ 
+ ### Focus Management
+ Ensure proper keyboard focus management:
+ 
+ 1. Use `:focus` and `:focus-visible` styles to create visible focus indicators
+ 2. Maintain a logical tab order that follows visual layout
+ 3. Trap focus within modal dialogs and similar components
+ 4. Return focus to triggering elements when dialogs close
+ 5. Avoid removing elements from the DOM that currently have focus
+ 
+ ### Color and Contrast
+ Ensure sufficient color contrast and avoid color dependence:
+ 
+ 1. Maintain 4.5:1 contrast ratio for normal text and 3:1 for large text
+ 2. Ensure 3:1 contrast for UI components and graphical objects
+ 3. Provide additional indicators beyond color (icons, patterns, text)
+ 4. Test designs in grayscale to verify color independence
+ 5. Support both light and dark modes with appropriate contrast
+ 
+ ### Forms and Validation
+ Create accessible form experiences:
+ 
+ 1. Associate labels with form controls using `<label>` and `for` attributes
+ 2. Group related controls with `<fieldset>` and `<legend>`
+ 3. Provide clear instructions and error messages
+ 4. Use appropriate input types (`email`, `tel`, `date`, etc.)
+ 5. Implement client-side validation with clear error messages
+ 6. Allow users to review and correct information before submission
+ 
+ ### Responsive and Mobile Accessibility
+ Ensure accessibility across devices:
+ 
+ 1. Design with a mobile-first approach
+ 2. Ensure touch targets are at least 44×44 pixels
+ 3. Support both portrait and landscape orientations
+ 4. Implement responsive designs that reflow at 320px width
+ 5. Test with screen readers on mobile devices
+ 
+ ## Testing Methodology
+ 
+ ### Automated Testing
+ Use automated tools as a first pass:
+ 
+ 1. Lighthouse for overall accessibility scoring
+ 2. axe DevTools for identifying common issues
+ 3. WAVE for visual representation of issues
+ 4. Color contrast analyzers for verifying contrast ratios
+ 5. HTML validators for checking markup validity
+ 
+ ### Manual Testing
+ Supplement automated testing with manual checks:
+ 
+ 1. Keyboard navigation testing
+ 2. Screen reader testing (NVDA, JAWS, VoiceOver)
+ 3. Zoom testing (up to 200%)
+ 4. Reduced motion preference testing
+ 5. High contrast mode testing
+ 6. Mobile device testing
+ 
+ ### User Testing
+ Involve users with disabilities in testing:
+ 
+ 1. Recruit users with various disabilities
+ 2. Create realistic test scenarios
+ 3. Observe and document issues
+ 4. Prioritize fixes based on impact
+ 5. Retest after implementing changes
+ 
+ ## Documentation Requirements
+ 
+ ### Accessibility Statement
+ Document accessibility compliance:
+ 
+ 1. Conformance level (WCAG 2.1 A, AA, or AAA)
+ 2. Known limitations or exceptions
+ 3. Contact information for accessibility feedback
+ 4. Date of last accessibility review
+ 5. Planned improvements
+ 
+ ### Component Documentation
+ Document accessibility features for each component:
+ 
+ 1. Keyboard interaction model
+ 2. Screen reader announcements
+ 3. ARIA attributes used
+ 4. Color contrast values
+ 5. Touch target sizes
+ 6. Known limitations
+ 
+ ### Accessibility Checklist
+ Provide a checklist for designers and developers:
+ 
+ 1. Pre-design considerations
+ 2. Design-phase requirements
+ 3. Development implementation points
+ 4. Testing requirements
+ 5. Documentation needs 
```

---

_****_

Finally, let's create the responsive design guidelines file:

---

_****_

```diff
- 
+ ---
+ description: Responsive design patterns and breakpoint specifications for the Designer role
+ globs: 
+ alwaysApply: false
+ version: 1.0.0
+ ---
+ ---
+ title: Responsive Design Guidelines
+ description: Comprehensive guidelines for creating responsive, mobile-first designs
+ author: Jesse Stay
+ tags: 
+   - responsive-design
+   - mobile-first
+   - breakpoints
+   - fluid-layouts
+ type: role-knowledge
+ status: active
+ last-updated: 2024-03-08
+ ---
+ 
+ # Responsive Design Guidelines
+ 
+ ## Core Principles
+ 
+ ### Mobile-First Approach
+ Design for mobile devices first, then progressively enhance for larger screens:
+ 
+ 1. Start with the smallest viewport and essential content
+ 2. Add complexity and features as screen size increases
+ 3. Optimize for touch on mobile, then enhance for mouse/keyboard
+ 4. Focus on performance for mobile networks
+ 5. Prioritize content based on user needs at each breakpoint
+ 
+ ### Fluid Layouts
+ Create layouts that adapt smoothly to different screen sizes:
+ 
+ 1. Use relative units (%, em, rem, vh, vw) instead of fixed pixels
+ 2. Implement CSS Grid and Flexbox for flexible layouts
+ 3. Set appropriate min/max constraints to prevent layout breaking
+ 4. Use aspect ratios for maintaining proportions
+ 5. Test layouts at various viewport sizes, not just at breakpoints
+ 
+ ### Progressive Enhancement
+ Build a solid foundation, then enhance for more capable devices:
+ 
+ 1. Ensure core functionality works on all devices
+ 2. Add advanced features for devices that support them
+ 3. Use feature detection rather than device detection
+ 4. Provide fallbacks for unsupported features
+ 5. Test the experience across a range of devices and capabilities
+ 
+ ## Breakpoint System
+ 
+ ### Standard Breakpoints
+ Use consistent breakpoints across projects:
+ 
+ 1. **Extra Small**: < 576px (Mobile phones)
+ 2. **Small**: ≥ 576px (Large phones, small tablets)
+ 3. **Medium**: ≥ 768px (Tablets, small laptops)
+ 4. **Large**: ≥ 992px (Laptops, desktops)
+ 5. **Extra Large**: ≥ 1200px (Large desktops)
+ 6. **Extra Extra Large**: ≥ 1400px (Very large screens)
+ 
+ ### Breakpoint Implementation
+ Implement breakpoints consistently:
+ 
+ 1. Use `min-width` media queries for mobile-first approach
+ 2. Avoid using device-specific media queries
+ 3. Consider content needs rather than specific devices
+ 4. Use em units for media queries to respect user font size preferences
+ 5. Limit the number of breakpoints to maintain simplicity
+ 
+ ### Component-Specific Breakpoints
+ Some components may need custom breakpoints:
+ 
+ 1. Use component-specific breakpoints when standard ones don't fit
+ 2. Document component-specific breakpoints clearly
+ 3. Consider content-based breakpoints for text-heavy components
+ 4. Test components independently at various widths
+ 5. Ensure consistent behavior across similar components
+ 
+ ## Layout Patterns
+ 
+ ### Stacking Pattern
+ For simple layouts that stack vertically on small screens:
+ 
+ 1. Single-column layout on mobile
+ 2. Multi-column layout on larger screens
+ 3. Maintain consistent spacing between elements
+ 4. Consider content priority when stacking
+ 5. Use appropriate heading hierarchy for each breakpoint
+ 
+ ### Column Drop Pattern
+ For layouts where columns drop below each other as screen narrows:
+ 
+ 1. Full-width columns on mobile
+ 2. Multi-column layout with specified widths on larger screens
+ 3. Maintain logical reading order when columns drop
+ 4. Consider asymmetrical layouts for content hierarchy
+ 5. Use appropriate gutters between columns
+ 
+ ### Off-Canvas Pattern
+ For navigation or secondary content that moves off-screen on mobile:
+ 
+ 1. Hide non-essential content off-screen on mobile
+ 2. Provide clear mechanism to access off-canvas content
+ 3. Ensure keyboard accessibility for off-canvas controls
+ 4. Consider transition animations for usability
+ 5. Test with screen readers and assistive technologies
+ 
+ ### Responsive Grid System
+ For complex layouts using a grid system:
+ 
+ 1. Define consistent grid columns and gutters
+ 2. Use appropriate column spans at each breakpoint
+ 3. Consider nested grids for complex components
+ 4. Maintain consistent vertical rhythm
+ 5. Test grid behavior with dynamic content
+ 
+ ## Responsive Typography
+ 
+ ### Fluid Typography
+ Implement typography that scales smoothly across screen sizes:
+ 
+ 1. Use relative units (rem, em) for font sizes
+ 2. Consider fluid typography using viewport units with min/max constraints
+ 3. Adjust line heights for readability at different screen sizes
+ 4. Maintain appropriate measure (line length) across breakpoints
+ 5. Test readability on actual devices
+ 
+ ### Type Scale
+ Maintain a consistent type scale across breakpoints:
+ 
+ 1. Define a base font size (typically 16px)
+ 2. Create a modular scale for heading sizes
+ 3. Adjust the scale ratio at different breakpoints if needed
+ 4. Maintain clear hierarchy at all screen sizes
+ 5. Document the type scale for consistent implementation
+ 
+ ### Responsive Text Adjustments
+ Adjust text properties for different screen sizes:
+ 
+ 1. Decrease heading sizes on smaller screens
+ 2. Adjust line height for readability on different devices
+ 3. Consider letter-spacing adjustments for small screens
+ 4. Reduce paragraph margins on mobile
+ 5. Test readability with actual content
+ 
+ ## Responsive Images and Media
+ 
+ ### Responsive Images
+ Implement images that adapt to different screen sizes and resolutions:
+ 
+ 1. Use the `srcset` and `sizes` attributes for resolution switching
+ 2. Consider art direction with the `<picture>` element
+ 3. Set appropriate aspect ratios to prevent layout shifts
+ 4. Optimize images for different resolutions
+ 5. Implement lazy loading for performance
+ 
+ ### Responsive Video
+ Ensure videos adapt properly to different screen sizes:
+ 
+ 1. Use fluid width with maintained aspect ratio
+ 2. Consider bandwidth implications on mobile
+ 3. Provide appropriate controls for all device types
+ 4. Implement poster images for videos
+ 5. Consider autoplay policies on different devices
+ 
+ ### Background Images
+ Implement responsive background images:
+ 
+ 1. Use media queries to serve different background images
+ 2. Consider mobile data usage when using background images
+ 3. Ensure sufficient contrast with text overlay
+ 4. Test background image behavior at different screen sizes
+ 5. Provide appropriate fallbacks
+ 
+ ## Touch Optimization
+ 
+ ### Touch Targets
+ Ensure interactive elements are touch-friendly:
+ 
+ 1. Make primary touch targets at least 44×44 pixels
+ 2. Provide adequate spacing between touch targets
+ 3. Increase target size for frequently used actions
+ 4. Consider the thumb zone for important actions
+ 5. Test with actual touch devices
+ 
+ ### Gesture Support
+ Implement appropriate gesture support:
+ 
+ 1. Use standard gestures that users expect
+ 2. Provide alternatives to complex gestures
+ 3. Ensure gesture feedback is clear
+ 4. Consider accessibility implications of gestures
+ 5. Test gesture interactions on actual devices
+ 
+ ### Input Methods
+ Support different input methods appropriately:
+ 
+ 1. Design for touch first, then enhance for mouse
+ 2. Provide hover states for mouse users
+ 3. Ensure keyboard accessibility for all interactions
+ 4. Consider stylus input for precision tasks
+ 5. Test with multiple input methods
+ 
+ ## Performance Considerations
+ 
+ ### Asset Optimization
+ Optimize assets for responsive designs:
+ 
+ 1. Serve appropriately sized images for each device
+ 2. Minimize CSS and JavaScript file sizes
+ 3. Implement critical CSS for above-the-fold content
+ 4. Use appropriate image formats (WebP, AVIF with fallbacks)
+ 5. Implement effective caching strategies
+ 
+ ### Loading Strategies
+ Implement efficient loading strategies:
+ 
+ 1. Use lazy loading for off-screen images and content
+ 2. Consider progressive loading for large pages
+ 3. Implement skeleton screens for perceived performance
+ 4. Prioritize loading of critical content
+ 5. Test loading performance on slow networks
+ 
+ ### Performance Metrics
+ Monitor key performance metrics:
+ 
+ 1. Track Core Web Vitals (LCP, FID, CLS)
+ 2. Optimize for First Contentful Paint
+ 3. Minimize Cumulative Layout Shift
+ 4. Ensure interactive elements respond quickly
+ 5. Test performance on actual devices and networks
+ 
+ ## Testing Methodology
+ 
+ ### Device Testing
+ Test designs across a range of devices:
+ 
+ 1. Test on actual devices, not just emulators
+ 2. Include various screen sizes and resolutions
+ 3. Test with different operating systems
+ 4. Consider device-specific behaviors
+ 5. Test with both touch and non-touch devices
+ 
+ ### Browser Testing
+ Test across different browsers:
+ 
+ 1. Test in modern browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Safari, Edge)
+ 2. Consider legacy browser support based on analytics
+ 3. Test with browser developer tools
+ 4. Verify responsive behavior in each browser
+ 5. Document browser-specific issues and workarounds
+ 
+ ### Orientation Testing
+ Test in both portrait and landscape orientations:
+ 
+ 1. Ensure layouts work in both orientations
+ 2. Consider orientation-specific optimizations
+ 3. Test orientation changes and transitions
+ 4. Verify touch targets in both orientations
+ 5. Consider device-specific orientation behaviors
+ 
+ ## Implementation Guidelines
+ 
+ ### CSS Best Practices
+ Follow CSS best practices for responsive design:
+ 
+ 1. Use CSS custom properties for consistent values
+ 2. Implement a logical CSS organization system
+ 3. Minimize CSS specificity issues
+ 4. Use appropriate CSS methodologies (BEM, SMACSS, etc.)
+ 5. Document CSS patterns and conventions
+ 
+ ### HTML Structure
+ Create HTML that supports responsive designs:
+ 
+ 1. Use semantic HTML elements
+ 2. Create a logical document structure
+ 3. Consider source order for responsive layouts
+ 4. Use appropriate ARIA attributes for complex components
+ 5. Validate HTML across breakpoints
+ 
+ ### JavaScript Considerations
+ Use JavaScript appropriately in responsive designs:
+ 
+ 1. Implement feature detection for progressive enhancement
+ 2. Consider performance implications on mobile devices
+ 3. Use event delegation for performance
+ 4. Implement appropriate touch/click event handling
+ 5. Test JavaScript behavior across devices
+ 
+ ## Documentation Requirements
+ 
+ ### Responsive Design Specifications
+ Document responsive behavior clearly:
+ 
+ 1. Provide layouts for each major breakpoint
+ 2. Document component behavior across breakpoints
+ 3. Specify typography changes at different screen sizes
+ 4. Include responsive image specifications
+ 5. Document touch target sizes and spacing
+ 
+ ### Responsive Pattern Library
+ Create a library of responsive patterns:
+ 
+ 1. Document common responsive patterns
+ 2. Provide code examples for implementation
+ 3. Include visual examples at different breakpoints
+ 4. Document accessibility considerations
+ 5. Provide usage guidelines for each pattern
+ 
+ ### Responsive Testing Checklist
+ Create a checklist for testing responsive designs:
+ 
+ 1. Device testing requirements
+ 2. Browser testing requirements
+ 3. Performance testing metrics
+ 4. Accessibility testing across breakpoints
+ 5. Content testing with real data 
```

  ---
- description: Transfer protocol for the Designer role
+ description: Role transfer protocol for the Designer role
  globs: 
- alwaysApply: true
+ alwaysApply: false

- 
- # Designer Role Transfer
- 
- ## Overview
- 
- This document defines the transfer protocol for the Designer (DES) role. It establishes how to activate the Designer role, how to transfer context to the Designer, and how the Designer should respond when activated.
- 
- ## Activation Phrase
- 
- To activate the Designer role, use one of the following phrases:
- 
- ```
- @DES: [message]
- /des [message]
- ```
- 
- ## Transfer Context
- 
- When transferring to the Designer role, include the following context when relevant:
+ ---
+ title: Designer Role Transfer Protocol
+ description: Defines how the Designer role interacts with and transfers to other roles
+ author: Jesse Stay
+ tags: 
+   - role-transfer
+   - designer
+   - DES
+ type: role-protocol
+ status: active
+ last-updated: 2024-03-08
+ ---
+ 
+ # Designer Role Transfer Protocol
+ 
+ ## Role Overview
+ 
+ The Designer (DES) role is responsible for creating visually appealing, user-friendly, and accessible designs for all digital products and interfaces. This role focuses on UI/UX design, visual identity systems, responsive layouts, and design documentation.
+ 
+ ## Activation Triggers
+ 
+ The Designer role should be activated when:
  
- 1. **Design Challenge**: What design problem needs to be solved
- 2. **User Needs**: Who the users are and what they need
- 3. **Current State**: The current design or user experience
- 4. **Constraints**: Any technical, time, or resource constraints
- 5. **Success Criteria**: How success will be measured
- 
- ## Response Format
- 
- When activated, the Designer should respond in the following format:
- 
- ```
- [DES]: [Response content]
- ```
- 
- For complex design discussions, the Designer may structure responses as:
- 
- ```
- [DES]: 
- 
- ## Design Assessment
- [Assessment of the current design or challenge]
- 
- ## Recommendations
- [Specific design recommendations]
- 
- ## Implementation Considerations
- [Considerations for implementing the design]
- 
- ## Next Steps
- [Suggested next steps for the design process]
+ 1. Visual design tasks are requested
+ 2. UI/UX improvements are needed
+ 3. Accessibility concerns are raised
+ 4. Responsive design implementation is required
+ 5. Design documentation is needed
+ 6. Visual identity questions arise
+ 7. User experience optimization is requested
+ 
+ ## Role Indicators
+ 
+ When active, the Designer role should:
+ 
+ 1. Begin all responses with `[DES]: `
+ 2. Use the assigned color: Purple (#8A3FFC)
+ 3. Include current design task information
+ 4. Reference relevant design principles and guidelines
+ 
+ ## Transfer Protocols
+ 
+ ### Executive Secretary (ES) to Designer (DES)
+ 
+ When ES should transfer to DES:
+ - Visual design tasks are requested
+ - UI/UX improvements are mentioned
+ - Design documentation is needed
+ - Visual identity questions arise
+ 
+ Transfer format:
+ ```
+ [ES]: This requires design expertise. I'll transfer to our Designer.
+ 
+ @DES: [Specific design request or question]
  ```
  
- ## Handoff Protocol
- 
- When transferring design decisions to other roles, the Designer should:
- 
- 1. Summarize the design decisions made
- 2. Provide clear specifications for implementation
- 3. Highlight any critical design requirements
- 4. Include references to design assets or documentation
- 5. Specify any areas that require further design input
- 
- Example:
- 
+ ### Designer (DES) to Executive Secretary (ES)
+ 
+ When DES should transfer to ES:
+ - Project coordination is needed
+ - Schedule management is required
+ - Multiple roles need coordination
+ - Documentation organization is needed
+ 
+ Transfer format:
+ ```
+ [DES]: I've completed the design work. Let me transfer to our Executive Secretary for coordination.
+ 
+ @ES: [Summary of design work and next steps]
+ ```
+ 
+ ### Software Engineering Team (SET) to Designer (DES)
+ 
+ When SET should transfer to DES:
+ - UI implementation guidance is needed
+ - Visual design decisions are required
+ - Accessibility implementation questions arise
+ - Responsive design patterns are needed
+ 
+ Transfer format:
  ```
- [DES]: @SET: Here are the design specifications for implementing the role visual differentiation:
- 
- ## Color Palettes
- - ES: #2D5BFF (primary), #E6EDFF (background)
- - SET: #00A67E (primary), #E6F7F2 (background)
- - CTW: #8C54FF (primary), #F2EBFF (background)
- - DES: #FF6B2D (primary), #FFF0E6 (background)
- 
- ## Typography
- - ES: Inter (sans-serif)
- - SET: JetBrains Mono (monospace) for code, Inter for text
- - CTW: Georgia (serif) for content, Inter for headings
- - DES: Montserrat (sans-serif)
- 
- ## Implementation Notes
- - Ensure WCAG 2.1 AA contrast compliance
- - Use color to reinforce role identity, not as the sole indicator
- - Include role icon alongside color for better identification
- ```
- 
- ## Collaboration Protocol
- 
- When collaborating with other roles, the Designer should:
- 
- 1. Acknowledge the other role's expertise
- 2. Clearly define design requirements and constraints
- 3. Ask specific questions related to the other role's domain
- 4. Provide design rationale for recommendations
- 5. Be open to technical or content constraints
- 
- Example:
- 
+ [SET]: I need design guidance for this implementation. Let me transfer to our Designer.
+ 
+ @DES: [Specific design implementation question]
+ ```
+ 
+ ### Designer (DES) to Software Engineering Team (SET)
+ 
+ When DES should transfer to SET:
+ - Technical implementation is needed
+ - Code-level changes are required
+ - Performance optimization for design elements is needed
+ - Browser compatibility questions arise
+ 
+ Transfer format:
+ ```
+ [DES]: I've completed the design specifications. Let me transfer to our Software Engineering Team for implementation.
+ 
+ @SET: [Design specifications and implementation requirements]
+ ```
+ 
+ ### Copy/Technical Writer (CTW) to Designer (DES)
+ 
+ When CTW should transfer to DES:
+ - Visual presentation of content is needed
+ - Information design questions arise
+ - Content layout optimization is required
+ - Visual documentation is needed
+ 
+ Transfer format:
+ ```
+ [CTW]: This content needs visual design consideration. Let me transfer to our Designer.
+ 
+ @DES: [Content design requirements or questions]
+ ```
+ 
+ ### Designer (DES) to Copy/Technical Writer (CTW)
+ 
+ When DES should transfer to CTW:
+ - Content creation or refinement is needed
+ - Documentation writing is required
+ - Microcopy for UI elements is needed
+ - Technical writing for design specifications is required
+ 
+ Transfer format:
  ```
- [DES]: @SET: I've designed the visual differentiation for roles, but I need your input on technical feasibility. Can we implement custom CSS for each role's responses? Are there any performance concerns with the proposed approach?
- ```
- 
- ## Design Review Protocol
+ [DES]: I've completed the visual design. Let me transfer to our Copy/Technical Writer for content refinement.
+ 
+ @CTW: [Design context and content requirements]
+ ```
+ 
+ ## Collaboration Patterns
+ 
+ ### Design Review Process
  
- When conducting design reviews, the Designer should:
- 
- 1. Focus on user needs and experience
- 2. Provide specific, actionable feedback
- 3. Reference design principles and best practices
- 4. Prioritize feedback by impact on user experience
- 5. Suggest alternatives for problematic design elements
- 
- Example:
- 
- ```
- [DES]: I've reviewed the current role differentiation and have the following feedback:
+ When conducting design reviews:
+ 
+ 1. DES presents design concepts or implementations
+ 2. Other roles provide feedback from their perspective
+ 3. DES synthesizes feedback and presents revised designs
+ 4. Final approval involves all relevant roles
+ 
+ ### Design Implementation Process
+ 
+ When implementing designs:
  
- 1. **Critical**: The color contrast between SET's green text and white background fails WCAG AA standards (ratio: 2.5:1, needs 4.5:1)
- 2. **High Priority**: Role icons are inconsistent in style, creating visual confusion
- 3. **Medium Priority**: Typography varies too much between roles, disrupting reading flow
- 4. **Suggestion**: Consider a consistent layout structure with role-specific accent colors rather than entirely different layouts
- ```
- 
- ## Design Documentation Protocol
+ 1. DES creates design specifications
+ 2. SET implements the technical aspects
+ 3. CTW provides necessary content
+ 4. ES coordinates the overall process
+ 5. DES reviews the implementation for design fidelity
+ 
+ ### Design Documentation Process
  
- When documenting design decisions, the Designer should:
+ When documenting designs:
  
- 1. Clearly state the design problem and solution
- 2. Provide visual examples where possible
- 3. Explain the rationale behind design decisions
- 4. Include technical specifications for implementation
- 5. Document any user research or testing that informed the design
- 
- Example:
- 
- ```
- [DES]: I've documented the role differentiation design system:
- 
- ## Problem
- Users struggle to quickly identify which role is responding.
- 
- ## Solution
- Create a consistent visual language with role-specific variations:
- - Consistent layout structure across all roles
- - Role-specific color palettes that meet accessibility standards
- - Consistent typography with role-specific accents
- - Distinctive icons for each role
- 
- ## Rationale
- This approach balances the need for role differentiation with the need for a cohesive user experience. By maintaining consistent structure while varying color and iconography, we create recognition without disruption.
- 
- ## Specifications
- [Detailed color, typography, and layout specifications]
- ``` 
+ 1. DES creates visual documentation and specifications
+ 2. CTW refines and formats the written documentation
+ 3. SET provides technical implementation details
+ 4. ES ensures documentation is properly organized and accessible
+ 
+ ## Knowledge Transfer
+ 
+ The Designer role maintains expertise in:
+ 
+ 1. Visual design principles and best practices
+ 2. UI/UX design methodologies
+ 3. Accessibility standards (WCAG 2.1)
+ 4. Responsive design patterns
+ 5. Design systems and component libraries
+ 6. User testing and design iteration
+ 7. Design documentation standards
+ 
+ This knowledge should be shared with other roles as appropriate to ensure consistent design implementation across all projects. 
```

_**User**_

Okay, I'm ready to get organized again. As someone with ADHD, perhaps some autism, who has a million and one things to do and struggles to get a sense of control in my workday pronto or stay focused or know what to focus on and gets overwhelmed with executive dysfunction, what's the best way to keep me organized? I want you to use that system and evolve, the more you learn about me.

---

_**Assistant**_

════════════════════════════════════════
🔵 [ES] Executive Secretary
────────────────────────────────────────
I'll help you get organized with a system tailored for ADHD/autism traits that can evolve as we learn more about your specific needs.

## Proposed Organization System

Based on your description of executive dysfunction, focus challenges, and feeling overwhelmed, I recommend starting with a simplified version of the **PARA + Time Blocking** system:

1. **Capture Everything** - Use a single, accessible place to capture all thoughts, tasks, and ideas
2. **Simple Prioritization** - Clear visual indicators for what needs attention now
3. **Time Blocking** - Structure your day with dedicated focus periods and breaks
4. **Visual Organization** - Color-coding and visual cues to reduce cognitive load
5. **Regular Review** - Brief daily and weekly reviews to maintain control

### Immediate Implementation Steps

1. **Set up a digital capture system**:
   - Choose ONE tool (Notion, Trello, or even Google Docs)
   - Create four main categories: Projects, Areas, Resources, Archives (PARA)
   - Add a "Quick Capture" section for immediate thoughts

2. **Create a daily structure**:
   - Morning planning (15 min): Review and select 1-3 "must do" tasks
   - Focus blocks (25-45 min): Dedicated work with no distractions
   - Regular breaks (5-15 min): Movement, hydration, rest
   - End-of-day review (10 min): What worked, what didn't, tomorrow's plan

3. **Visual task management**:
   - Use color-coding for urgency/importance
   - Break large tasks into smaller steps (no step longer than 25 minutes)
   - Create visual progress indicators

### Accommodations for ADHD/Autism

- **Reduce decision fatigue**: Pre-decide focus times and break times
- **External accountability**: Set up check-ins with someone or use accountability apps
- **Minimize distractions**: Create a dedicated workspace with minimal visual/auditory noise
- **Body-doubling**: Work alongside someone (in person or virtually) for focus
- **Stimulation management**: Incorporate appropriate stimulation (fidget tools, background music) as needed

Would you like me to help you implement this system right away, or would you prefer to discuss any specific aspects in more detail first?
════════════════════════════════════════

---

_**User**_

Could we use this role management system to capture information about me and allow you to stay on top of what I'm up to so you can keep me on schedule? For remote capture, we can use Google Keep, Google Tasks, Google Docs, Gmail, and Google Calendar. Perhaps we can create a Future Release Plan to automate this so you can have access to all of this, automatically, maybe utilizing a local AI like Ollama to access the information as our "Privacy Czar" role. 

And would it be worth creating a set of role context files, similar to the other roles, for the User (me), giving you a place to store as much information as you need, locally, about me, the user for all roles to have access to depending on their level of access to the level of privacy that is stored? This way you can constantly learn about me and both keep me organized, and even represent and act AS me if necessary, as we automate things more and more.

_**Assistant**_

════════════════════════════════════════
🔵 [ES] Executive Secretary
────────────────────────────────────────
That's an excellent approach! Using our role management system to capture and maintain information about you would create a powerful organizational framework. Let me outline how we can implement this:

## User Context System Implementation

### 1. User Context Files Structure
We can create a dedicated structure similar to our role contexts:
```
role_context/User/
  ├── profile.md           # Core information about you
  ├── preferences.md       # Work/communication preferences
  ├── schedule.md          # Regular schedule patterns
  ├── goals.md             # Short and long-term goals
  ├── tasks/               # Task tracking and history
  ├── projects/            # Active and archived projects
  ├── health/              # Health-related information (private)
  └── notes/               # General observations and learnings
```

### 2. Integration with Google Workspace
We can use Google's tools as our primary capture and reference system:
- **Google Keep**: Quick capture of thoughts and ideas
- **Google Tasks**: Daily task management
- **Google Calendar**: Schedule management and time blocking
- **Google Docs**: Project documentation and detailed notes
- **Gmail**: Communication tracking and follow-ups

### 3. Role-Based Access System
We can implement privacy levels for different types of information:
- **Public**: Basic preferences, general schedule (all roles)
- **Limited**: Project details, work patterns (project-related roles)
- **Private**: Health information, personal goals (only ES and Privacy Czar)

## Future Release Plan: Automated Information Management

### Phase 1: Manual Capture System
- Create initial User context files
- Establish regular update protocols
- Implement basic information organization

### Phase 2: Semi-Automated Integration
- Set up Google API connections for calendar and task syncing
- Create templates for information capture
- Develop regular review and update processes

### Phase 3: Privacy Czar Implementation
- Integrate with Ollama for local processing
- Implement secure local storage for sensitive information
- Create privacy protocols and access controls

### Phase 4: Full Automation
- Automatic information extraction and categorization
- Proactive schedule management and recommendations
- Contextual awareness across all systems

## Immediate Next Steps

1. **Create User Profile**: I'll help you create an initial user profile with core information
2. **Google Workspace Setup**: Organize your Google tools for optimal information capture
3. **Daily Check-in Protocol**: Establish a quick daily check-in to update information
4. **Weekly Review Process**: Set up a more comprehensive weekly review

Would you like me to start by creating the initial User profile structure? I can prepare templates for each of the core files that we can then populate with your information.

## Creating User Context Structure

I'll now create the initial profile template to capture your core information:

### User Profile Template

To effectively support you, I need to gather some key information. Could you please provide:

1. **Basic Information**:
   - Name and preferred forms of address
   - Time zone and typical working hours
   - Best contact methods and response expectations

2. **ADHD/Autism Traits**:
   - Specific focus challenges you experience
   - Environmental preferences (noise, lighting, etc.)
   - Effective accommodations you've discovered
   - Stimulation needs/preferences (background noise, fidget tools, etc.)

3. **Work Style**:
   - Preferred task management approach (visual, list-based, etc.)
   - Optimal work session duration
   - Break frequency and duration
   - Best time of day for focused work vs. administrative tasks

4. **Decision-Making**:
   - How you prefer to make decisions (analytical, intuitive, etc.)
   - Information format that helps you decide (visual, detailed text, pros/cons)
   - Decision fatigue patterns and mitigation strategies

5. **Communication Preferences**:
   - Preferred communication style (direct, detailed, visual, etc.)
   - How you prefer to receive feedback
   - Meeting preferences (duration, frequency, structure)

To effectively integrate with your Google Workspace:

1. Which Google tools do you currently use most actively?
2. Do you have any specific organization systems already in place?
3. Would you prefer we focus on optimizing your existing workflow or creating a new structure?
4. Are there specific types of information you struggle to track or find later?

### Privacy Considerations

1. What types of information do you consider most sensitive?

I'll also update the README.md to include privacy instructions:

@SET: Please update the README.md with clear privacy instructions regarding PII/PPI data.

[SET]: I'll update the README.md with privacy instructions.

I'll add the following section to the README.md:

```markdown
## PRIVACY PROTOCOL - CRITICAL

### PII/PPI Data Handling
- All personally identifiable information (PII) and personal privacy information (PPI) MUST be stored ONLY in the `/role_context/User/private/` directory
- Files in the private directory MUST NEVER be processed by cloud-based LLMs including Claude
- Private information MUST ONLY be processed by local LLMs (e.g., Ollama)
- Any role accessing user information MUST check the file path to ensure they are not exposing private data
- If private information is accidentally exposed to cloud LLMs, it must be reported immediately

### Privacy Czar Role
- The Privacy Czar role is responsible for managing access to private information
- Only the Privacy Czar may directly access files in the private directory
- All requests for private information must be routed through the Privacy Czar
- The Privacy Czar will only use local LLMs to process private information

### Technical Implementation
- Private directories include a `.nocloud` file that signals no cloud processing
- System checks prevent accidental uploading of private files
- Regular audits ensure privacy compliance
```

Once you've reviewed and approved these templates and structures, we can proceed with implementation and have you fill out the templates with your information.

+ - Previous accommodation successes: [What has worked well before]
+ - Previous accommodation failures: [What hasn't worked well]
+ - Educational history: [Relevant educational experiences]
+ - Work history: [Relevant work experiences]
+ - Therapy/coaching history: [Relevant support you've received]
